     <p>
      <b>
       Jack White
      </b>
      (born
      <b>
       John Anthony Gillis
      </b>
      ; July 9, 1975)
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      is an American musician, record producer, and occasional actor. He is best known as the lead singer and guitarist of
      <a href="/wiki/The_White_Stripes" title="The White Stripes">
       The White Stripes
      </a>
      , although he has had success in other bands and as a solo artist. On April 24, 2012, White released his debut solo album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Blunderbuss_(album)" title="Blunderbuss (album)">
        Blunderbuss
       </a>
      </i>
      . His second studio album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Lazaretto_(album)" title="Lazaretto (album)">
        Lazaretto
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released on June 10, 2014. Both received wide commercial and critical acclaim.
     </p>
     <p>
      After moonlighting in several underground Detroit bands as a drummer, White founded The White Stripes with fellow Detroit nativeand then wife
      <a href="/wiki/Meg_White" title="Meg White">
       Meg White
      </a>
      in 1997. Their 2001 breakthrough album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/White_Blood_Cells_(album)" title="White Blood Cells (album)">
        White Blood Cells
       </a>
      </i>
      , brought them international fame with the hit single and accompanying music video, "
      <a href="/wiki/Fell_in_Love_with_a_Girl" title="Fell in Love with a Girl">
       Fell in Love with a Girl
      </a>
      ". This recognition provided White opportunities to collaborate with famous artists, including Loretta Lynn and Bob Dylan.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2006, White founded
      <a href="/wiki/The_Raconteurs" title="The Raconteurs">
       The Raconteurs
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Benson" title="Brendan Benson">
       Brendan Benson
      </a>
      , and in 2009 founded
      <a href="/wiki/The_Dead_Weather" title="The Dead Weather">
       The Dead Weather
      </a>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Alison_Mosshart" title="Alison Mosshart">
       Alison Mosshart
      </a>
      of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Kills" title="The Kills">
       The Kills
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      White has enjoyed consistent critical and popular success, and is widely credited as one of the key artists in the
      <a href="/wiki/Garage_rock#Revivals" title="Garage rock">
       garage rock revival
      </a>
      of the 2000s. He has won eight Grammy Awards, and both of his solo albums have reached number one on the Billboard charts.
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      ranked him number 70 on its 2010 list of "The 100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time".
      <a href="/wiki/David_Fricke" title="David Fricke">
       David Fricke
      </a>
      's 2011 list ranked him at number 17. White has an extensive collection of guitars and other instruments, and has a preference for vintage items that often have connections to famous blues artists. He is a vocal advocate for analog technology and recording techniques, and he is a board member of the
      <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">
       Library of Congress
      </a>
      '
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Recording_Preservation_Foundation" title="National Recording Preservation Foundation">
       National Recording Preservation Foundation
      </a>
      . His record label and studio
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Man_Records" title="Third Man Records">
       Third Man Records
      </a>
      releases
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vinyl_recording" title="Vinyl recording">
       vinyl recordings
      </a>
      of his own work, as well as that of other artists and local school children.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His latest album holds the record for most first-week vinyl sales since 1991.
     </p>
     <p>
      White values his privacy and has been known to create misdirection about his personal life; he has been called "eccentric." He and Meg divorced in 2000. He married the model and singer
      <a href="/wiki/Karen_Elson" title="Karen Elson">
       Karen Elson
      </a>
      in 2005, though they divorced in 2013. Together, they have a son and daughter. He currently resides in
      <a href="/wiki/Nashville,_Tennessee" title="Nashville, Tennessee">
       Nashville, Tennessee
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

           <span class="toctext">

           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7">
        <a href="#Third_Man_Records">
         <span class="tocnumber">
          3
         </span>

        </a>
       </li>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">
       Early life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      John Anthony Gillis
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dunn166_5-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-dunn166-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      was born in
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">
       Detroit
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Michigan" title="Michigan">
       Michigan
      </a>
      , the youngest of ten childrenand the seventh sonof Teresa (ne Bandyk) and Gorman M. Gillis.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramedina_6-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lauramedina-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gormang_7-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gormang-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His mother's family was
      <a href="/wiki/Poles" title="Poles">
       Polish
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-male_8-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-male-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      while his father was of
      <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">
       Scottish
      </a>
      -Canadian descent.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wooing_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wooing-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He was raised a
      <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
       Catholic
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and his father and mother both worked for the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archdiocese_of_Detroit" title="Archdiocese of Detroit">
       Archdiocese of Detroit
      </a>
      (as the Building Maintenance Superintendent and secretary in the Cardinal's office, respectively).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gillis became an
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Altar_boy" title="Altar boy">
       altar boy
      </a>
      , which landed him an uncredited role in the 1987 movie
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Rosary_Murders" title="The Rosary Murders">
        The Rosary Murders
       </a>
      </i>
      , filmed mainly at
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holy_Redeemer_Church_(Detroit)" title="Holy Redeemer Church (Detroit)">
       Holy Redeemer
      </a>
      parish in southwest Detroit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Gillis' early musical influences were inherited from his older brothers, and he learned to play the instruments they abandoned;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eels_13-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-eels-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      he began playing the drums in the first grade after finding a kit in the attic.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramedina_6-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-lauramedina-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eels_13-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-eels-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JW_14-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-JW-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a child, he was a fan of classical music,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOTB16_15-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SOTB16-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but in elementary school, he began listening to
      <a href="/wiki/The_Doors" title="The Doors">
       the Doors
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd" title="Pink Floyd">
       Pink Floyd
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Led_Zeppelin" title="Led Zeppelin">
       Led Zeppelin
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccollum_16-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mccollum-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a "shorthaired [teenager] with braces,"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SOTB16_15-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SOTB16-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Gillis began listening to the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blues_music" title="Blues music">
       blues
      </a>
      and 1960s rock that would influence him in The White Stripes,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with
      <a href="/wiki/Son_House" title="Son House">
       Son House
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Blind_Willie_McTell" title="Blind Willie McTell">
       Blind Willie McTell
      </a>
      being among his favorite blues guitarists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He has said in interviews that
      <a href="/wiki/Son_House" title="Son House">
       Son House
      </a>
      's "Grinnin' In Your Face" is his favorite song of all time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NB_18-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NB-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a drummer, his heroes include
      <a href="/wiki/Gene_Krupa" title="Gene Krupa">
       Gene Krupa
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Copeland" title="Stewart Copeland">
       Stewart Copeland
      </a>
      , and Crow Smith from
      <a href="/wiki/Flat_Duo_Jets" title="Flat Duo Jets">
       Flat Duo Jets
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moderndrummer_19-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-moderndrummer-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2005 on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">
        60 Minutes
       </a>
      </i>
      , he told
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mike_Wallace_(journalist)" title="Mike Wallace (journalist)">
       Mike Wallace
      </a>
      that his life could have turned out differently. "I'd got accepted to a seminary in
      <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin" title="Wisconsin">
       Wisconsin
      </a>
      , and I was gonna become a priest, but at the last second I thought, 'I'll just go to public school.' I had just gotten a new amplifier in my bedroom, and I didn't think I was allowed to take it with me."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBS_20-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CBS-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Instead, he got accepted into the famed
      <a href="/wiki/Cass_Technical_High_School" title="Cass Technical High School">
       Cass Technical High School
      </a>
      as a business major, and played the drums and trombone in the band.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CASS_22-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-CASS-22">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        22
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      At 15, Gillis began a three-year
      <a href="/wiki/Upholstery" title="Upholstery">
       upholstery
      </a>
      apprenticeship with a family friend, Brian Muldoon.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He credits Muldoon with exposing him to punk music as they worked together in the shop.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Muldoon goaded his young apprentice into forming a band: "He played drums," Gillis thought. "Well I guess I'll play guitar then."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imgl_23-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-imgl-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The two recorded an album,
      <i>
       Makers of High Grade Suites,
      </i>
      as
      <a href="/wiki/The_Upholsterers" title="The Upholsterers">
       the Upholsterers
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      As a senior in high school, he met Megan White at the Memphis Smoke restaurant where she worked,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
       <a href="#cite_note-24">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        24
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and they frequented the coffee shops, local music venues, and record stores of the area.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
       <a href="#cite_note-25">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        25
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After a courtship, they got married on September 21, 1996.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside32_26-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside32-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-White_Stripes_Marriage_License_27-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-White_Stripes_Marriage_License-27">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        27
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a reversal of tradition, he took her last name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
       <a href="#cite_note-29">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        29
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      After completing his apprenticeship, he started a one-man business of his own, Third Man Upholstery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Believer_30-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Believer-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The slogan of his business was "Your Furniture's Not Dead" and the color scheme was yellow and blackincluding a yellow van, a yellow-and-black uniform, and a yellow clipboard.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Believer_30-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Believer-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Although Third Man Upholstery never lacked business, he claims it was unprofitable due to his complacency about money and his business practices that were perceived as unprofessional, including making bills out in crayon and writing poetry inside the furniture.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Believer_30-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Believer-30">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        30
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Career">
       Career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_White_Stripes">
       The White Stripes
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The White Stripes">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/The_White_Stripes" title="The White Stripes">
       The White Stripes
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tleft">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jack_%26_Meg,_The_White_Stripes.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2569" data-file-width="3058" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg/220px-Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg/330px-Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg/440px-Jack_%26_Meg%2C_The_White_Stripes.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jack_%26_Meg,_The_White_Stripes.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        At the O2
        <a href="/wiki/Wireless_Festival" title="Wireless Festival">
         Wireless Festival
        </a>
        in 2007
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      At 19 years old, Jack had landed his first professional gig as the drummer for the Detroit band
      <a href="/wiki/Goober_%26_the_Peas" title="Goober &amp; the Peas">
       Goober &amp; the Peas
      </a>
      , and was still in that position when the band broke up in 1996.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
       <a href="#cite_note-31">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        31
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was in this band that he learned about touring and performing onstage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      After the split, he settled into working as an upholsterer by day while moonlighting in local bands, as well as performing solo shows.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside32_26-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside32-26">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        26
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Though a bartender by trade,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Meg began to learn to play the drums in 1997 and, according to Jack, "When she started to play drums with me, just on a lark, it felt liberating and refreshing."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The couple became a band, calling themselves The White Stripes,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside_33-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and two months later performed their first show.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Despite being married, Jack and Meg publicly presented themselves as siblings,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mick_34-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-mick-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powers_35-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-powers-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and keeping to a chromatic theme, dressed only in red, white, and black.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
       <a href="#cite_note-37">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        37
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They began their career as part of the Michigan's
      <a href="/wiki/Underground_music" title="Underground music">
       underground
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Garage_rock" title="Garage rock">
       garage rock
      </a>
      music scene.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They played along with and opened for more established local bands such as
      <a href="/wiki/Bantam_Rooster" title="Bantam Rooster">
       Bantam Rooster
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Dirtbombs" title="The Dirtbombs">
       the Dirtbombs
      </a>
      , Two Star Tabernacle, Rocket 455, and the Hentchmen, among others.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 1998, the White Stripes were signed to
      <a href="/wiki/Italy_Records" title="Italy Records">
       Italy Records
      </a>
      a small and
      <a href="/wiki/Independent_record_label" title="Independent record label">
       independent
      </a>
      Detroit-based garage
      <a href="/wiki/Punk_rock" title="Punk rock">
       punk
      </a>
      labelby Dave Buick.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
       <a href="#cite_note-38">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        38
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The band released its
      <a href="/wiki/The_White_Stripes_(album)" title="The White Stripes (album)">
       eponymous debut album
      </a>
      in 1999, and a year later the album was followed up by the cult classic,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
       <a href="#cite_note-39">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        39
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/De_Stijl_(album)" title="De Stijl (album)">
        De Stijl
       </a>
      </i>
      . The album eventually peaked at number 38 in
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_(magazine)" title="Billboard (magazine)">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
      </a>
      's
      <a href="/wiki/Independent_Albums" title="Independent Albums">
       Independent Albums
      </a>
      chart.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 2001 the band released
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/White_Blood_Cells_(album)" title="White Blood Cells (album)">
        White Blood Cells
       </a>
      </i>
      . The album's stripped-down garage rock sound drew critical acclaim in the US and beyond,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      making The White Stripes one of the more acclaimed bands of 2002,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and forefront figures in the garage band revival of the time.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside_33-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside-33">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        33
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RSB_40-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-RSB-40">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        40
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/John_Peel" title="John Peel">
       John Peel
      </a>
      , an influential DJ and the band's early advocate in the UK, said they were the most exciting thing he'd heard since Jimi Hendrix.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWEET_41-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-SWEET-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      said of White, "beneath the arty facade lies one of the most cagey, darkly original rockers to come along since
      <a href="/wiki/Kurt_Cobain" title="Kurt Cobain">
       Kurt Cobain
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hagan_42-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-hagan-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was followed up in 2003 by the commercially and critically successful
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Elephant_(album)" title="Elephant (album)">
        Elephant
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
       <a href="#cite_note-43">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        43
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
       <a href="#cite_note-44">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        44
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
       <a href="#cite_note-45">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        45
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">
       Allmusic
      </a>
      wrote that the album "sounds even more pissed-off, paranoid and stunning than its predecessor ... darker and more difficult than
      <i>
       White Blood Cells
      </i>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
       <a href="#cite_note-46">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        46
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album's first single, "
      <a href="/wiki/Seven_Nation_Army" title="Seven Nation Army">
       Seven Nation Army
      </a>
      ", became the band's signature song,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
       <a href="#cite_note-47">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        47
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      reaching number one on the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Modern_Rock_Tracks" title="Billboard Modern Rock Tracks">
       Billboard Modern Rock Tracks
      </a>
      chart for three weeks, winning the 2004
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Song">
       Grammy Award for Best Rock Song
      </a>
      , and becoming an international sporting and protest anthem.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DN_48-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DN-48">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        48
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The band's fifth album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Get_Behind_Me_Satan" title="Get Behind Me Satan">
        Get Behind Me Satan
       </a>
      </i>
      , was recorded in White's own home and marked a change in the band's musical direction, with piano-driven melodies and experimentation with
      <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">
       marimba
      </a>
      and a more rhythm-based guitar playing by White.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The band's sixth album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Icky_Thump" title="Icky Thump">
        Icky Thump
       </a>
      </i>
      , was released in 2007 and, unlike their previous
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lo-fi" title="Lo-fi">
       lo-fi
      </a>
      albums, it was recorded in Nashville at Blackbird Studio.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was regarded as a return to the band's earlier blues and garage-rock sound.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changing_50-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-changing-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It debuted at number two on the US
      <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200">
       <i>
        Billboard
       </i>
       200
      </a>
      chart, and entered the
      <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">
       UK Albums Chart
      </a>
      at number one, selling over 300,000 vinyl copies in England alone.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinyl_51-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinyl-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
       <a href="#cite_note-52">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        52
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Of his excitement for vinyl, White explained, "We can't afford to lose the feeling of cracking open a new record and looking at large artwork and having something you can hold in your hands."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinyl_51-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinyl-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In support of the album, they launched a Canadian tour, in which they played a gig in every one of the country's provinces and territories. However, later that year, the band announced the cancellation of 18 tour dates due to Meg's struggle with acute
      <a href="/wiki/Anxiety_disorder" title="Anxiety disorder">
       anxiety
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
       <a href="#cite_note-53">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        53
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A few days later, the duo cancelled the remainder of their 2007 UK tour dates as well.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cancel_54-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cancel-54">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        54
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      White worked with other artists in the meantime, but revealed the band's plan to release a seventh album by the summer of 2009.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
       <a href="#cite_note-55">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        55
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
       <a href="#cite_note-56">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        56
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On February 20, 2009and on the final episode of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Late_Night_with_Conan_O%27Brien" title="Late Night with Conan O'Brien">
        Late Night with Conan O'Brien
       </a>
      </i>
      the band made their first live appearance after the cancellation of the tour,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
       <a href="#cite_note-57">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        57
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a documentary about their Canadian tourtitled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Under_Great_White_Northern_Lights" title="Under Great White Northern Lights">
        The White Stripes: Under Great White Northern Lights
       </a>
      </i>
      debuted later that year at the
      <a href="/wiki/Toronto_International_Film_Festival" title="Toronto International Film Festival">
       Toronto International Film Festival
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
       <a href="#cite_note-58">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        58
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, almost two years passed with no new releases, and on February 2, 2011, the band reported on their official website that they were disbanding. White emphasized that it was not due to health issues or artistic differences, "but mostly to preserve what is beautiful and special about the band."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
       <a href="#cite_note-59">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        59
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Raconteurs">
       The Raconteurs
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: The Raconteurs">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/The_Raconteurs" title="The Raconteurs">
       The Raconteurs
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Raconteurs,_Stockholm.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="681" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg/220px-Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg/330px-Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/76/Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg/440px-Raconteurs%2C_Stockholm.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Raconteurs,_Stockholm.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Brendan Benson and Jack White
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In 2005, while collaborating with
      <a href="/wiki/Brendan_Benson" title="Brendan Benson">
       Brendan Benson
      </a>
      a fellow Michigan native whom White had worked with before
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      they composed a song called "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steady,_as_She_Goes" title="Steady, as She Goes">
       Steady, as She Goes
      </a>
      ." This inspired them to create a full band, and they invited
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jack_Lawrence_(bassist)" title="Jack Lawrence (bassist)">
       Jack Lawrence
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Keeler" title="Patrick Keeler">
       Patrick Keeler
      </a>
      of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greenhornes" title="Greenhornes">
       Greenhornes
      </a>
      to join them in what would become The Raconteurs. The musicians met in Benson's home studio in Detroit and, for the remainder of the year, they recorded when time allowed. The result was the band's debut album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Broken_Boy_Soldiers" title="Broken Boy Soldiers">
        Broken Boy Soldiers
       </a>
      </i>
      . Reaching the Top Ten charts in both the US and the UK,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lauramedina_6-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-lauramedina-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      it was nominated for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album" title="Best Rock Album">
       Best Rock Album
      </a>
      at the 2006 Grammy Awards. The lead single, "
      <a href="/wiki/Steady,_As_She_Goes" title="Steady, As She Goes">
       Steady, As She Goes
      </a>
      " was nominated for
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance_by_a_Duo_or_Group_with_Vocal" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal">
       Best Rock Performance by a Duo or Group with Vocal
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammymuseum_60-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-grammymuseum-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The Raconteurs set out on tour to support the album,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including eight dates as the opening act for
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      . The group's second album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Consolers_of_the_Lonely" title="Consolers of the Lonely">
        Consolers of the Lonely
       </a>
      </i>
      , and its first single, "
      <a href="/wiki/Salute_Your_Solution" title="Salute Your Solution">
       Salute Your Solution
      </a>
      ", were released simultaneously in 2008. The album reached number seven on the Billboard 200 chart, and received a Grammy nomination for
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album" title="Best Rock Album">
       Best Rock Album
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-grammymuseum_60-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-grammymuseum-60">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        60
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Dead_Weather">
       The Dead Weather
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: The Dead Weather">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/The_Dead_Weather" title="The Dead Weather">
       The Dead Weather
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2232" height="322" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg/220px-The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg/330px-The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/42/The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg/440px-The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Dead_Weather_Glastonbury_2009-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Jack White and Alison Mosshart performing live with the Dead Weather at the
        <a href="/wiki/Glastonbury_Festival" title="Glastonbury Festival">
         Glastonbury Festival
        </a>
        , June 26, 2009.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      While on tour to promote
      <i>
       Consolers of the Lonely
      </i>
      , White developed bronchitis and often lost his voice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Allison Mosshart, the frontwoman for the
      <a href="/wiki/The_Kills" title="The Kills">
       The Kills
      </a>
      (who was touring with the Raconteurs at the time) would often fill in as his vocal replacement.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The chemistry between the two artists led them to collaborate, and in early 2009, White formed a new group called
      <a href="/wiki/The_Dead_Weather" title="The Dead Weather">
       the Dead Weather
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Mosshart sang and White took drum and vocal duties, while the Raconteurs bassist Jack Lawrence and
      <a href="/wiki/Queens_of_the_Stone_Age" title="Queens of the Stone Age">
       Queens of the Stone Age
      </a>
      keyboardist and guitarist
      <a href="/wiki/Dean_Fertita" title="Dean Fertita">
       Dean Fertita
      </a>
      rounded out the four-piece.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
       <a href="#cite_note-61">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        61
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The group debuted a handful of new tracks on March 11, 2009 in Nashville from their debut album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Horehound_(album)" title="Horehound (album)">
        Horehound
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
       <a href="#cite_note-62">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        62
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It came out on July 13, 2009 in Europe and July 14, 2009 in North America on White's Third Man Records label.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
       <a href="#cite_note-63">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        63
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
       <a href="#cite_note-64">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        64
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In October 2009, Mosshart confirmed that the second album was "halfway done,"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
       <a href="#cite_note-65">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        65
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the first single, "Die by the Drop," was released on March 30, 2010.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
       <a href="#cite_note-66">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        66
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The new album (again on the Third Man Records label) was titled
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Cowards" title="Sea of Cowards">
        Sea of Cowards
       </a>
      </i>
      and was released on May 7 of that year in Ireland, on May 10 in the United Kingdom, and on May 11 in the U.S.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
       <a href="#cite_note-67">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        67
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Solo_career">
       Solo career
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Solo career">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      White's popular and critical success with The White Stripes enabled him to collaborate as a solo artist with other musicians. He has joined other artists on their recordings, as well as invited artists to perform on his projects. He has also worked as a producer for various artists, often through his label, Third Man Records.
     </p>
     <p>
      Rumors began to circulate in 2003 that White had collaborated with
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_Six" title="Electric Six">
       Electric Six
      </a>
      for their song "
      <a href="/wiki/Danger!_High_Voltage" title="Danger! High Voltage">
       Danger! High Voltage
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FW_68-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-FW-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He and the Electric Six both denied this,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FW_68-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-FW-68">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        68
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside182_69-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside182-69">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        69
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the vocal work was credited officially to John S O'Leary.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
       <a href="#cite_note-70">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        70
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In subsequent interviews with Chris Handyside, however,
      <a href="/wiki/Tyler_Spencer" title="Tyler Spencer">
       Dick Valentine
      </a>
      and Corey Martin (Electric Six band members) acknowledged White's involvement and confirmed that he received no payment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-handyside180_71-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-handyside180-71">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        71
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      White worked with
      <a href="/wiki/Loretta_Lynn" title="Loretta Lynn">
       Loretta Lynn
      </a>
      on her 2004 album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Van_Lear_Rose" title="Van Lear Rose">
        Van Lear Rose
       </a>
      </i>
      , which he produced and performed on.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_72-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was a critical and commercial success.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2008, White collaborated with
      <a href="/wiki/Alicia_Keys" title="Alicia Keys">
       Alicia Keys
      </a>
      on the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Another_Way_to_Die" title="Another Way to Die">
       Another Way to Die
      </a>
      ", the theme song for the
      <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">
       James Bond
      </a>
      film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_of_Solace" title="Quantum of Solace">
        Quantum of Solace
       </a>
      </i>
      . In 2009, Jack White was featured in
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/It_Might_Get_Loud" title="It Might Get Loud">
        It Might Get Loud
       </a>
       ,
      </i>
      a film in which he,
      <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Page" title="Jimmy Page">
       Jimmy Page
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/The_Edge" title="The Edge">
       The Edge
      </a>
      come together to discuss the electric guitar and each artist's different playing methods.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cieply_73-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-cieply-73">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        73
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White's first solo single, "
      <a href="/wiki/Fly_Farm_Blues" title="Fly Farm Blues">
       Fly Farm Blues
      </a>
      ," was written and recorded in 10 minutes during the filming of the movie that August.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lyda_74-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-lyda-74">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        74
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The single went on sale as a 7-inch vinyl record from Third Man Records and as a digital single available through
      <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">
       iTunes
      </a>
      on August 11. In November 2010, producer
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danger_Mouse_(music_producer)" title="Danger Mouse (music producer)">
       Danger Mouse
      </a>
      announced that Whitealong with
      <a href="/wiki/Norah_Jones" title="Norah Jones">
       Norah Jones
      </a>
      had been recruited for his collaboration with
      <a href="/wiki/Daniele_Luppi" title="Daniele Luppi">
       Daniele Luppi
      </a>
      entitled
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rome_(album)" title="Rome (album)">
        Rome
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
       <a href="#cite_note-75">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        75
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White provided vocals to three songs on the album: "The Rose with the Broken Neck," "Two Against One," and "The World."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
       <a href="#cite_note-76">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        76
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White finished and performed the song "You Know That I Know", and it was featured on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/The_Lost_Notebooks_of_Hank_Williams" title="The Lost Notebooks of Hank Williams">
        The Lost Notebooks of Hank Williams
       </a>
      </i>
      , released on October 4, 2011. In that same year, he produced and played on
      <a href="/wiki/Wanda_Jackson" title="Wanda Jackson">
       Wanda Jackson
      </a>
      's album
      <i>
       Let's Have a Party
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_72-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inskeep_77-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-inskeep-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      To her delight, his studio also released the album on a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/45_rpm_single#Types" title="45 rpm single">
       7-inch vinyl
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inskeep_77-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-inskeep-77">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        77
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      White has worked with other artists as well, including
      <a href="/wiki/Beck" title="Beck">
       Beck
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">
       the Rolling Stones
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Beck" title="Jeff Beck">
       Jeff Beck
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">
       <a href="#cite_note-78">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        78
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      On January 30, 2012 White released "
      <a href="/wiki/Love_Interruption" title="Love Interruption">
       Love Interruption
      </a>
      " as the first single off his debut, self-produced solo album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Blunderbuss_(album)" title="Blunderbuss (album)">
        Blunderbuss
       </a>
      </i>
      , which was released on April 24, 2012.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79">
       <a href="#cite_note-79">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        79
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In support of the album, he appeared on
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">
        Saturday Night Live
       </a>
      </i>
      as the musical guest and played at select festivals during the summer of 2012, including the Firefly Music Festival,
      <a href="/wiki/Radio_1%27s_Big_Weekend" title="Radio 1's Big Weekend">
       Radio 1's Hackney Weekend
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Sasquatch!_Music_Festival" title="Sasquatch! Music Festival">
       Sasquatch! Music Festival
      </a>
      , the
      <a href="/wiki/Fuji_Rock_Festival" title="Fuji Rock Festival">
       Fuji Rock Festival
      </a>
      in Japan (one of the biggest festivals in the world), and
      <a href="/wiki/Rock_Werchter" title="Rock Werchter">
       Rock Werchter
      </a>
      in Belgium. Later in the year, he headlined
      <a href="/wiki/Austin_City_Limits_Music_Festival" title="Austin City Limits Music Festival">
       Austin City Limits Music Festival
      </a>
      . During his tour for the album, White employed two live bands, which he alternated between at random. The first, called The Peacocks, was all female and consisted of
      <a href="/wiki/Ruby_Amanfu" title="Ruby Amanfu">
       Ruby Amanfu
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Carla_Azar" title="Carla Azar">
       Carla Azar
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Lillie_Mae_Rische&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Lillie Mae Rische (page does not exist)">
       Lillie Mae Rische
      </a>
      , Maggie Bjorklund,
      <a href="/wiki/Brooke_Waggoner" title="Brooke Waggoner">
       Brooke Waggoner
      </a>
      , and alternating bassists
      <a href="/wiki/Bryn_Davies" title="Bryn Davies">
       Bryn Davies
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Popper" title="Catherine Popper">
       Catherine Popper
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-flotat_80-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-flotat-80">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        80
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The other, The Buzzards, was all male and consisted of Daru Jones, Dominic Davis,
      <a href="/wiki/Fats_Kaplin" title="Fats Kaplin">
       Fats Kaplin
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ikey_Owens" title="Ikey Owens">
       Ikey Owens
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cory_Younts" title="Cory Younts">
       Cory Younts
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tweeting_81-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-tweeting-81">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        81
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White said maintaining two bands was too expensive,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and abandoned the practice at the conclusion of the tour.
      <i>
       Blunderbluss
      </i>
      was ultimately nominated for several Grammys, including Album of the Year, Best Rock Album, and Best Rock Song for "Freedom at 21."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On April 1, 2014, White announced his second solo album,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Lazaretto_(album)" title="Lazaretto (album)">
        Lazaretto
       </a>
      </i>
      , inspired by plays and poetry he had written as a teen.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">
       <a href="#cite_note-82">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        82
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinylrecord_83-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinylrecord-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was released on June 10, 2014 simultaneously with the first single off the album, "High Ball Stepper." The album debuted at number one on the Billboard 200 chart and,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinylrecord_83-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinylrecord-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in a personal triumph for White,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinylrecord_83-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinylrecord-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      broke the record for the largest sales week for a vinyl album since SoundScan began tracking sales in 1991.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinylrecord_83-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinylrecord-83">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        83
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The album was widely praised among critics, and was nominated for three Grammy Awards:
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Alternative Music Album">
       Best Alternative Music Album
      </a>
      , as well as
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Song" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Song">
       Best Rock Song
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Performance" title="Grammy Award for Best Rock Performance">
       Best Rock Performance
      </a>
      (for the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Lazaretto_(song)" title="Lazaretto (song)">
       Lazaretto
      </a>
      "). During the supporting tour, he performed the longest show of his career on July 30, 2014 at the
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Masonic_Temple" title="Detroit Masonic Temple">
       Detroit Masonic Temple
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">
       <a href="#cite_note-84">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        84
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and later performed as one of the headliners at the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coachella_Festival" title="Coachella Festival">
       Coachella Festival
      </a>
      over two weekends in April 2015.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
       <a href="#cite_note-85">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        85
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On April 14, 2015, White announced that the festival would be his last electrice set, followed by one acoustic show in each of the five U.S. states he had yet to perform in, before he would be taking a prolonged break from live performances.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
       <a href="#cite_note-86">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        86
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
       <a href="#cite_note-87">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        87
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="574" data-file-width="1178" height="107" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg/220px-Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg/330px-Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/3d/Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg/440px-Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jack_White_as_Elvis_in_Walk_Hard.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        White (opposite
        <a href="/wiki/John_C._Reilly" title="John C. Reilly">
         John C. Reilly
        </a>
        ) portraying
        <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">
         Elvis Presley
        </a>
        in the satirical 2007 film
        <i>
         Walk Hard.
        </i>
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      White has also had a minor acting career. He appeared in the 2003 film
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_Mountain_(movie)" title="Cold Mountain (movie)">
       <i>
        Cold Mountain
       </i>
      </a>
      as a character named Georgia and performed five songs for the
      <a href="/wiki/Cold_Mountain_(soundtrack)" title="Cold Mountain (soundtrack)">
       <i>
        Cold Mountain
       </i>
       soundtrack
      </a>
      : "Sittin' on Top of the World", "Wayfaring Stranger", "Never Far Away", "Christmas Time Soon Will Be Over" and "Great High Mountain." The 2003
      <a href="/wiki/Jim_Jarmusch" title="Jim Jarmusch">
       Jim Jarmusch
      </a>
      film
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Coffee_and_Cigarettes" title="Coffee and Cigarettes">
        Coffee and Cigarettes
       </a>
      </i>
      featured both Jack and Meg in the segment "Jack Shows Meg His Tesla Coil." He also played
      <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">
       Elvis Presley
      </a>
      in the 2007 satire
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walk_Hard" title="Walk Hard">
        Walk Hard
       </a>
      </i>
      .
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Third_Man_Records">
       Third Man Records
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Third Man Records">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Man_Records" title="Third Man Records">
       Third Man Records
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      White founded Third Man Records in 2001.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
       <a href="#cite_note-88">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        88
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, it was not until after he moved to Nashville that White purchased a space in 2009 to house his label.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He explained, "For the longest time I did not want to have my own studio gear, mostly because with the White Stripes I wanted to have the constriction of going into a studio and having a set time of 10 days or two weeks to finish an album, and using whatever gear they happen to have there. After 10 to 15 years of recording like that I felt that it was finally time for me to have my own place to produce music, and have exactly what I want in there: the exact tape machines, the exact microphones, the exact amplifiers that I like, and so on."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jack_.26_White_Vision_89-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jack_.26_White_Vision-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Using the slogan Your Turntables Not Dead,"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eels_13-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-eels-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Third Man also presses vinyl records,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vinyl_51-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-vinyl-51">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        51
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      for the artists on its label, for White's own musical ventures, as well as for third parties for hire.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wtfthirdman_90-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wtfthirdman-90">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        90
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In March 2015, Third Man joined in the launch of
      <a href="/wiki/Tidal_(service)" title="Tidal (service)">
       TIDAL
      </a>
      , a music streaming service that
      <a href="/wiki/Jay_Z" title="Jay Z">
       Jay Z
      </a>
      purchased and co-owns with other major music artists.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
       <a href="#cite_note-91">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        91
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
       <a href="#cite_note-92">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        92
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Later that year, White partnered with
      <a href="/wiki/Shinola" title="Shinola">
       Shinola
      </a>
      a watch manufacturerto open a retail location in Detroit.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-doerr_93-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-doerr-93">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        93
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Musical_equipment_and_sound">
       Musical equipment and sound
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Musical equipment and sound">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Instruments_and_equipment">
       Instruments and equipment
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Instruments and equipment">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      White owns many instruments and, historically, has tended to use certain ones for specific projects or in certain settings. He has a preference for vintage guitars, many of which are associated with influential blues artists. Much of his equipment is custom-made, for both technical and aesthetic reasons.
     </p>
     <p>
      During his career with The White Stripes, White principally used three guitars,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      though he used others as well.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarplayer_95-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-guitarplayer-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The red, "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JB_Hutto#Death_and_legacy" title="JB Hutto">
       JB Hutto
      </a>
      ,"
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/JB_Hutto_Montgomery_Airline" title="JB Hutto Montgomery Airline">
       Airline guitar
      </a>
      was a vintage 1964 model originally distributed by
      <a href="/wiki/Montgomery_Ward" title="Montgomery Ward">
       Montgomery Ward
      </a>
      department store.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Though used by several artists, White's attachment to the instrument raised its popularity to the extent that
      <a href="/wiki/Eastwood_Guitars" title="Eastwood Guitars">
       Eastwood Guitars
      </a>
      began producing a modified replica around 2000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The 1950s-era
      <a href="/wiki/Kay_Musical_Instrument_Company" title="Kay Musical Instrument Company">
       Kay
      </a>
      Hollowbody was a gift from his brother in return for a favor.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWEET_41-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-SWEET-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It was the same brand of electric guitar made popular by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Howling_Wolf" title="Howling Wolf">
       Howling Wolf
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and White most famously used it on "Seven Nation Army."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He began using a
      <a href="/wiki/Gibson_Guitar_Corporation_product_list#Acoustic_guitars" title="Gibson Guitar Corporation product list">
       1915 Gibson L-1 acoustic
      </a>
      (often called the
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Johnson" title="Robert Johnson">
       Robert Johnson
      </a>
      model) on the
      <i>
       Icky Thump
      </i>
      album;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      in an interview for Gibson, he called the instrument his favorite.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also used a three-pickup Airline Town &amp; Country (later featured in the "Steady As She Goes" music video),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a
      <a href="/wiki/Harmony_Company" title="Harmony Company">
       Harmony
      </a>
