      Rocket,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a 1970s-era
      <a href="/wiki/Epiphone_Crestwood" title="Epiphone Crestwood">
       Crestwood
      </a>
      Astral II,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and what would become the first of three custom Gretsch Rancher Falcon acoustic guitars.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      While with the Stripes, any equipment that did not match their red/black/white color scheme were painted red.
     </p>
     <p>
      While the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raconteurs" title="Raconteurs">
       Raconteurs
      </a>
      were still in development, White commissioned
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/luthier" title="wiktionary:luthier">
       luthier
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Randy_Parsons" title="Randy Parsons">
       Randy Parsons
      </a>
      to create what White called the
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch_Triple_Jet" title="Gretsch Triple Jet">
       Triple Jet
      </a>
      a custom guitar styled after the
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch#Solid_body_electric" title="Gretsch">
       Duo Jet
      </a>
      double-cutaway guitar.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premier_98-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-premier-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Parsons's first product was painted copper color, however he decided to create a second version with a completely copper body, which White began to use instead.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premier_98-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-premier-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the Raconteurs first tour, White also played a
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch#Current_models" title="Gretsch">
       Gretsch Anniversary Jr.
      </a>
      with a
      <a href="/wiki/Bigsby_vibrato_tailpiece" title="Bigsby vibrato tailpiece">
       Bigsby vibrato tailpiece
      </a>
      and three Filtertron pickups.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-premier_98-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-premier-98">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        98
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He later added a custom Gretsch Anniversary Jr. with two cutaways, a lever-activated mute system, a built-in and retractable bullet microphone, and a light-activated
      <a href="/wiki/Theremin" title="Theremin">
       theremin
      </a>
      next to the Bigsby.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White has dubbed this one the "Green Machine",
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and it is featured in
      <i>
       It Might Get Loud
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He sometimes played a
      <a href="/wiki/Gibson_J-160E" title="Gibson J-160E">
       Gibson J-160E
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      a
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch#Current_models" title="Gretsch">
       Gretsch Duo Jet
      </a>
      in Cadillac Green,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and a second
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch#Acoustic" title="Gretsch">
       Gretsch Rancher
      </a>
      acoustic guitar.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the Raconteurs' 2008 tour, he had
      <a href="/wiki/Analog_Man_(instrument_maker)" title="Analog Man (instrument maker)">
       Analog Man
      </a>
      plate all of his pedals in copper.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dolphin_99-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-dolphin-99">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        99
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He has since acquired another Gretsch, a custom white
      <a href="/wiki/Billy_Gibbons" title="Billy Gibbons">
       Billy Gibbons
      </a>
      /
      <a href="/wiki/Bo_Diddley" title="Bo Diddley">
       Bo Diddley
      </a>
      signature
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch_Jupiter_Thunderbird" title="Gretsch Jupiter Thunderbird">
       Gretsch Jupiter Thunderbird
      </a>
      with a gold double pickguard (as seen in the music video for "Another Way to Die").
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White found a
      <a href="/wiki/Gretsch#Solid_body_electric" title="Gretsch">
       1957 Gretsch G6134 White Penguin
      </a>
      in 2007 while on tour in Texas
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the same one he used in the music video for "
      <a href="/wiki/Icky_Thump_(song)" title="Icky Thump (song)">
       Icky Thump
      </a>
      "
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      which ultimately fit in with the Dead Weather's color scheme.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarplayer_95-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-guitarplayer-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also uses a black left-handed one since the Dead Weather album
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Sea_of_Cowards" title="Sea of Cowards">
        Sea of Cowards
       </a>
      </i>
      came out.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      He has also been known to play
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fender_Telecasters" title="Fender Telecasters">
       Fender Telecasters
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      featuring one in the music video for Loretta Lynn's "Portland, Oregon."
     </p>
     <p>
      White owns three Gretsch Rancher Falcons because he says that its bass tones make it his favorite acoustic to play live.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They are collectively referred to as his "girlfriends," as each one has an image of a classic movie star on the back.
      <a href="/wiki/Claudette_Colbert" title="Claudette Colbert">
       Claudette Colbert
      </a>
      is the brunette he used while with the Stripes,
      <a href="/wiki/Rita_Hayworth" title="Rita Hayworth">
       Rita Hayworth
      </a>
      is the redhead he acquired with the Raconteurs, and
      <a href="/wiki/Veronica_Lake" title="Veronica Lake">
       Veronica Lake
      </a>
      is the blonde he added in 2010 while with the Dead Weather.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-robinson_94-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-robinson-94">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        94
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <table class="mbox-small" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div class="center">
         <div class="floatnone">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </div>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
        <div class="haudio">
         <div style="padding:4px 0">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Seven_Nation_Army_(sample).ogg" title="File:Seven Nation Army (sample).ogg">
           "Seven Nation Army" excerpt
          </a>
         </div>
         <div>
          <div class="mediaContainer" style="position:relative;display:block;width:220px">

            <br/>

             download the clip
            </a>

            <a href="https://www.mediawiki.org/wiki/Special:MyLanguage/Extension:TimedMediaHandler/Client_download">

           </audio>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">
          Demonstrates the "fake" bass tone White achieves by using an octave pedal.
         </div>
        </div>
        <hr/>
       </td>
      </tr>
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em">
        <span>
         <i>
          Problems playing this file? See
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
           media help
          </a>
          .
         </i>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      White uses numerous effects to create his live sound, most notably a
      <a href="/wiki/DigiTech_Whammy" title="DigiTech Whammy">
       DigiTech Whammy WH-4
      </a>
      to create the rapid modulations in pitch he uses in his solos.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_100-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White also produces a "fake" bass tone by playing the Kay Hollowbody and JB Hutto Montgomery Airline guitars through a Whammy IV set to one octave down for a very thick, low, rumbling sound, which he uses most notably on the song "
      <a href="/wiki/Seven_Nation_Army" title="Seven Nation Army">
       Seven Nation Army
      </a>
      ".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_100-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also uses an MXR Micro Amp and custom Electro-Harmonix
      <a href="/wiki/Big_Muff" title="Big Muff">
       Big Muff
      </a>
      Distortion/Sustainer.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-equipboard_97-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-equipboard-97">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        97
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2005, for the single "Blue Orchid," White employed a
      <a href="/wiki/Electro-Harmonix" title="Electro-Harmonix">
       Electro-Harmonix
      </a>
      Polyphonic Octave Generator (POG), which let him mix in several octave effects into one along with the dry signal.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarplayer_95-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-guitarplayer-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He plugs this setup into a 1970s
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fender_Twin_Reverb" title="Fender Twin Reverb">
       Fender Twin Reverb
      </a>
      "Silverface" and two 100-Watt Sears
      <a href="/wiki/Silvertone_(instruments)" title="Silvertone (instruments)">
       Silvertone
      </a>
      1485 610 amplifiers.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarplayer_95-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-guitarplayer-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He also used a 1960s Fender Twin Reverb "Blackface".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gg_96-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-gg-96">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        96
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-guitarplayer_95-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-guitarplayer-95">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        95
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      On occasion, White also plays other instruments, such as a Black Gibson F-4
      <a href="/wiki/Mandolin" title="Mandolin">
       mandolin
      </a>
      ("Little Ghost"), piano (on most tracks from
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Get_Behind_Me_Satan" title="Get Behind Me Satan">
        Get Behind Me Satan
       </a>
      </i>
      , and various others), and an
      <a href="/wiki/Electric_piano" title="Electric piano">
       electric piano
      </a>
      on such tracks as "The Air Near My Fingers" and "I'm Finding it Harder to be a Gentleman". White also plays percussion instruments such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Marimba" title="Marimba">
       marimba
      </a>
      (as on "The Nurse"),
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      drums and
      <a href="/wiki/Tambourine" title="Tambourine">
       tambourine
      </a>
      . For The White Stripes' 2007 tour, he played a custom-finish Hammond A-100 organ with a Leslie 3300 speaker, which was subsequently loaned to
      <a href="/wiki/Bob_Dylan" title="Bob Dylan">
       Bob Dylan
      </a>
      , and currently resides at Third Man Studios.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
       <a href="#cite_note-101">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        101
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On the album
      <i>
       Broken Boy Soldiers
      </i>
      , both he and Benson are credited with playing the album's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Synth" title="Synth">
       synths
      </a>
      and organ.
     </p>
     <p>
      With the Dead Weather, White plays a custom Ludwig Classic Maple kit in Black Oyster Pearl.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moderndrummer_19-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-moderndrummer-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Notably, it includes two-snare drums, which White calls "the jazz canon."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-moderndrummer_19-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-moderndrummer-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For the 2009 Full Flash Blank tour, White used a drum head with the Three Brides of Dracula on the front, but in 2010, White employed a new drum head, upon the release of
      <i>
       Sea of Cowards
      </i>
      , which has an image of The Third Man himself: Harry Lime attempting to escape certain capture in the sewers of Vienna. During the American leg of the 2010 tour, White switched his drum head again featuring a picture of himself in the guise he wore on the cover of
      <i>
       Sea of Cowards
      </i>
      . This drum head is called Sam Kay by some fans, referring to the insert inside of the 12" LP.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Minimalist_style">
       Minimalist style
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Minimalist style">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:30em; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
       <div>
        <p>
         "I love analogue because of what it makes you do. Digital recording gives you all this freedom, all these options to change the sounds that you are putting down, and those are for the most part not good choices to have for an artist," and "Mechanics are always going to provide inherent little flaws and tiny little specks and hisses that will add to the idea of something beautiful, something romantic. Perfection, making things perfectly in time and perfectly free of extraneous noise, is not something to aspire to! Why would anyone to aspire to such a thing?"
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jack_.26_White_Vision_89-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-Jack_.26_White_Vision-89">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           89
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </p>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       Jack White
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      White has long been a proponent of analog equipment and the associated working methods.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_72-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-72">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        72
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Beginning in the fifth grade, he and his childhood friend, Dominic Suchyta, would listen to records in White's attic on weekends and began to record cover songs on an old
      <a href="/wiki/Multitrack_recording" title="Multitrack recording">
       four-track
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Reel_to_reel" title="Reel to reel">
       reel to reel
      </a>
      tape machine.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The White Stripes' first album was largely recorded in the attic of his parents' home.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCOLLUM_12-10">
       <a href="#cite_note-McCOLLUM-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As their fame grew beyond Detroit, the Stripes became known for their affected innocence and stripped-down playing style.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In particular, White became distinguished for his nasal vocal delivery and loose, explosive guitar delivery.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In an early
      <i>
       New York Times
      </i>
      concert review from 2001, Ann Powers said that, while White's playing was "ingenious," he "created more challenges by playing an acoustic guitar with paper taped over the hole and a less-than-high-quality solid body electric."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powers_35-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-powers-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      His home studio in Nashville contains two rooms ("I want everyone close, focused, feeling like we're in it together.")
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with two pieces of equipment: a Neve mixing console,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and two Studer A800 2-inch 8-track tape recorders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jack_.26_White_Vision_89-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-Jack_.26_White_Vision-89">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        89
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      In his introduction in the documentary film,
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/It_Might_Get_Loud" title="It Might Get Loud">
        It Might Get Loud
       </a>
      </i>
      , White showcases his minimalist style by constructing a guitar built out of a plank of wood, three nails, a glass
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coke_bottle" title="Coke bottle">
       Coke bottle
      </a>
      , a guitar string, and a pickup. He ends the demonstration by saying, "Who says you need to buy a guitar?"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imgl_23-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-imgl-23">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        23
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2012 episode of the show
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Portlandia_episodes#Season_3_.282012.E2.80.9313.29" title="List of Portlandia episodes">
        Portlandia
       </a>
      </i>
      , White made a cameo in a sketch spoofing home studio enthusiasts who prefer antique recording equipment.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
       <a href="#cite_note-102">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        102
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      For $300,000 in January 2015, an online bidder won an auction for Elvis Presley's first recording everan acetate of two cover songs: "My Happiness" and "That's When Your Heartaches Begin".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elvisauction_103-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-elvisauction-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elvisauction_103-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-elvisauction-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Almost two months later, in its edition of March 6,
      <i>
       Billboard
      </i>
      magazine announced the buyer had been White.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elvisauction_103-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-elvisauction-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The vinyl was recorded at SUN Records in Memphis, Tennessee in the summer of 1953 when Presley was 18 years old.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">
       Reception
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Reception">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      White has enjoyed both critical and popular success, and is widely credited as one of the key artists in the
      <a href="/wiki/Garage_rock#Revivals" title="Garage rock">
       garage rock revival
      </a>
      of the 2000s.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-leahey_2-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-leahey-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone_(magazine)" title="Rolling Stone (magazine)">
        Rolling Stone
       </a>
      </i>
      ranked him number 70 on its 2010 list of "The 100 Greatest Guitarists of All Time".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-greatguitarists_104-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-greatguitarists-104">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        104
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <a href="/wiki/David_Fricke" title="David Fricke">
       David Fricke
      </a>
      's 2011 list ranked him at number 17.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
       <a href="#cite_note-105">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        105
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He has won eight Grammy Awards and both of his solo albums have reached number one on the Billboard charts. Interviewers note the wide breadth of the music styles and eras he draws from for inspiration.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-boilen_106-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-boilen-106">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        106
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In May 2015, the
      <a href="/wiki/Music_City_Walk_of_Fame" title="Music City Walk of Fame">
       Music City Walk of Fame
      </a>
      announced that it would be honoring White (along with Loretta Lynn) with a medallion at its re-opening in Nashville.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
       <a href="#cite_note-107">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        107
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Much has been made of White's "showmanship" and affectations.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_100-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-NYT-100">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        100
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Since the beginning, critics have debated the "riddle" of White's self-awareness against his claims of authenticity,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-powers_35-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-powers-35">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        35
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hagan_42-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-hagan-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      with people falling on both sides of the issue. Joe Hagan of
      <i>
       The New York Times
      </i>
      asked in 2001, "Is Mr. White, a 25-year-old former upholsterer from southwest Detroit, concocting this stuff with a wink? Or are the White Stripes simply nave?"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hagan_42-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-hagan-42">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        42
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Alexis Petridis, of
      <i>
       The Guardian
      </i>
      , said that White "makes for an enigmatic figure. Not because he's particularly difficult or guarded, but simply because what he tells you suggests a lifelong penchant for inscrutable behaviour."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White himself confesses, "Sometimes I think I'm a simple guy, but I think the reality is I'm really complicated, as simple as I wish I was".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">
       Personal life
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Personal life">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      White is protective of his privacy and gives few details of his family life, even going as far as to disseminate false information.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He states that he does not consider his personal life relevant to his art, saying "It's the same thing as asking
      <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">
       Michelangelo
      </a>
      , 'What kind of shoes do you wear?'...In the end, it doesn't really matter ... the only thing that's going to be left is our records and photos."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWEET_41-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-SWEET-41">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        41
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Relationships">
       Relationships
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Relationships">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Meg_White.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="360" data-file-width="475" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Meg_White.jpg/220px-Meg_White.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Meg_White.jpg/330px-Meg_White.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Meg_White.jpg/440px-Meg_White.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Meg_White.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Drummer
        <a href="/wiki/Meg_White" title="Meg White">
         Meg White
        </a>
        , Jack's former bandmate and ex-wife.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Jack and Meg officially divorced on March 24, 2000.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GNdivorce_108-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-GNdivorce-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In 2003, he had a brief but relationship with actress
      <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9e_Zellweger" title="Rene Zellweger">
       Rene Zellweger
      </a>
      , whom he met during the filming of
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Cold_Mountain_(film)" title="Cold Mountain (film)">
        Cold Mountain
       </a>
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changing_50-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-changing-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      That summer, the couple were in a car accident in which White broke his left index finger and was forced to reschedule much of the summer tour.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
       <a href="#cite_note-109">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        109
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He posted the footage of his finger surgery on the web for fans.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
       <a href="#cite_note-110">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        110
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White and Zellweger's breakup became public in December 2004.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
       <a href="#cite_note-111">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        111
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      White met British model
      <a href="/wiki/Karen_Elson" title="Karen Elson">
       Karen Elson
      </a>
      when she appeared in The White Stripes music video for "
      <a href="/wiki/Blue_Orchid" title="Blue Orchid">
       Blue Orchid
      </a>
      ". The video's director,
      <a href="/wiki/Floria_Sigismondi" title="Floria Sigismondi">
       Floria Sigismondi
      </a>
      , noted "you sensed an energy between them".
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
       <a href="#cite_note-112">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        112
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DFP_113-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-DFP-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      They married on June 1, 2005, in
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manaus,_Brazil" title="Manaus, Brazil">
       Manaus, Brazil
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DFP_113-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-DFP-113">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        113
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The wedding took place in a canoe on the
      <a href="/wiki/Amazon_River" title="Amazon River">
       Amazon River
      </a>
      and was officiated by a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shaman" title="Shaman">
       shaman
      </a>
      . A Roman Catholic priest later
      <a href="/wiki/Validation_of_marriage" title="Validation of marriage">
       convalidated
      </a>
      their marriage.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_114-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-OS-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Manager Ian Montone was the best man and Meg White was the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maid_of_honor" title="Maid of honor">
       maid of honor
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_114-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-OS-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Official wedding announcements stated that "it was the first marriage" for both.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OS_114-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-OS-114">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        114
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On May 2, 2006, the couple had a daughter, Scarlett Teresa White.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KidName_115-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-KidName-115">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        115
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Their second child, Henry Lee White, was born on August 7, 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
       <a href="#cite_note-116">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        116
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The family resided in
      <a href="/wiki/Brentwood,_Tennessee" title="Brentwood, Tennessee">
       Brentwood
      </a>
      , a suburb south of Nashville,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">
       <a href="#cite_note-117">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        117
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      where Elson managed a vintage clothing store called
      <i>
       Venus &amp; Mars
      </i>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
       <a href="#cite_note-118">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        118
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_119-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-avclub-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Elson provided vocals on White's first solo record.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-avclub_119-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-avclub-119">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        119
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, the couple announced their intention to divorce in June 2011,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
       <a href="#cite_note-120">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        120
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      throwing "a positive swing bang humdinger" party to commemorate the split.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      On July 22, 2013, a Nashville judge barred White from having "any contact with Karen Elson whatsoever except as it relates to parenting time with the parties' minor children."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
       <a href="#cite_note-121">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        121
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      A counter-motion was filed on August 2, 2013, stating that "The reason for filing this response is that Mr. White does not want to be portrayed as something he is not, violent toward his wife and children."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
       <a href="#cite_note-122">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        122
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The divorce was finalized on November 26, 2013.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-divorcepaper_123-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-divorcepaper-123">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        123
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Elson later recanted the charges, attributing the "aggressive" proceedings to her divorce attorneys, and saying "those who gain of a marriage ending helped to create a downward spiral at my most vulnerable."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White agreed, saying, "When shitty lawyers are in a situation like divorce, their goal is to villainize."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The former couple reportedly remain on good terms.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id=".27Eccentricism.27">
       'Eccentricism'
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 'Eccentricism'">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      White has been called "
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/eccentric" title="wiktionary:eccentric">
       eccentric
      </a>
      ."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-changing_50-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-changing-50">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        50
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-storming_124-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-storming-124">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        124
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
       <a href="#cite_note-125">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        125
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thumpitup_126-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-thumpitup-126">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        126
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
       <a href="#cite_note-127">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        127
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He is known for creating mythology around his endeavors;
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wooing_9-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-wooing-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      examples include his claim that the Stripes began on
      <a href="/wiki/Bastille_Day" title="Bastille Day">
       Bastille Day
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      that he and Meg are the two youngest of ten siblings,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klosterman_32-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Klosterman-32">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        32
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mick_34-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-mick-34">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        34
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
       <a href="#cite_note-128">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        128
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and that Third Man Records used to be a candy factory.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eels_13-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-eels-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      These assertions came into question or were disproven, such as when, in 2002, the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Free_Press" title="Detroit Free Press">
        Detroit Free Press
       </a>
      </i>
      produced copies of both a marriage license and divorce certificate for him and Meg, confirming their history as a married couple.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GNdivorce_108-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-GNdivorce-108">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        108
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Neither addresses the truth officially, and Jack continues to refer to Meg as his sister in interviews,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-eels_13-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-eels-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      including in the documentary
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Under_Great_White_Northern_Lights" title="Under Great White Northern Lights">
        Under Great White Northern Lights
       </a>
      </i>
      , filmed in 2007.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wfp_129-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-wfp-129">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        129
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2005 interview with
      <i>
       Rolling Stone
      </i>
      magazine, Jack alluded to this
      <a href="/wiki/Open_secret" title="Open secret">
       open secret
      </a>
      , implying that it was intended to keep the focus on the music rather than the couple's relationship:
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       "When you see a band that is two pieces, husband and wife, boyfriend and girlfriend, you think, 'Oh, I see...' When they're brother and sister, you go, 'Oh, that's interesting.' You care more about the music, not the relationshipwhether they're trying to save their relationship by being in a band."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:350px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
       <div>
        <p>
         It became hypnotic. This was the minimum amount of staples I could put to hold this fabric down. The number three exemplifies the almost iconic, mysterious perfection that cannot be obtained...To this day, I still think about it all the time.
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-4">
          <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           49
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </p>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       White, on how seeing three staples on a upholstery piece triggered his affinity for the number three.
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      He has an attachment to the number three,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
       <a href="#cite_note-130">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        130
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      stemming from seeing three staples in the back of a
      <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Kagan" title="Vladimir Kagan">
       Vladimir Kagan
      </a>
      couch he helped to upholster as an apprentice.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-petridis_49-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-petridis-49">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        49
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      His business ventures frequently feature "three" in the title and he typically appends "III" to the end of his name.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      During the White Stripes 2005 tour in the UK, White began referring to himself as "Three Quid""
      <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quid" title="wiktionary:quid">
       quid
      </a>
      " being British slang for pound sterling.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NME_131-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-NME-131">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        131
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      He maintains an aesthetic that he says challenges whether people will believe he is "real."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He frequently color-codes his endeavors, such as the aforementioned Third Man Upholstery and The White Stripes, as well as Third Man Records, which is completely outfitted in yellow, black, red, and blue (including staff uniforms).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elvisauction_103-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-elvisauction-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      As a
      <a href="/wiki/Taxidermy" title="Taxidermy">
       taxidermy
      </a>
      enthusiastthat correlates to his work as an upholstererhe decorates his studio in preserved animals, including a peacock, giraffe, and Himalayan goat.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-elvisauction_103-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-elvisauction-103">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        103
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Controversy">
       Controversy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Controversy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      On December 13, 2003, White was involved in an altercation with
      <a href="/wiki/Jason_Stollsteimer" title="Jason Stollsteimer">
       Jason Stollsteimer
      </a>
      , lead singer of
      <a href="/wiki/The_Von_Bondies" title="The Von Bondies">
       the Von Bondies
      </a>
      , at the Magic Stick, a Detroit club.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
       <a href="#cite_note-132">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        132
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vonbondies_133-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-vonbondies-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White was charged with
      <a href="/wiki/Misdemeanor" title="Misdemeanor">
       misdemeanor
      </a>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aggravated_assault" title="Aggravated assault">
       aggravated assault
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
       <a href="#cite_note-134">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        134
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He pleaded guilty to the lesser charge of assault and
      <a href="/wiki/Battery_(crime)" title="Battery (crime)">
       battery
      </a>
      , was fined $750 (including court costs), and was sentenced to take
      <a href="/wiki/Anger_management" title="Anger management">
       anger management
      </a>
      classes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vonbondies_133-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-vonbondies-133">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        133
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:350px; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
      <div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
       <div>
        <p>
         "I so love your heart that burns
         <br/>
         That in your people's body yearns
         <br/>
         To perpetuate, and permeate, the lonely dream that does encapsulate,
         <br/>
         Your spirit, that God insulates,
         <br/>
         With courageous dream's concern"
         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccollum_16-1">
          <a href="#cite_note-mccollum-16">
           <span>
            [
           </span>
           16
           <span>
            ]
           </span>
          </a>
         </sup>
        </p>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div style="text-align: left;">
       Excerpt from "Courageous Dream's Concern," as published in the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Free_Press" title="Detroit Free Press">
         Detroit Free Press
        </a>
       </i>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      White has repeatedly referenced conflicts that erupted between him and fellow artists in Detroit's underground music scene after The White Stripes gained international success.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-WOW_3-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-WOW-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Killingsworth_36-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-Killingsworth-36">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        36
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In a 2006 interview with the
      <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">
       Associated Press
      </a>
      , he said that he eventually left Detroit because, "he could not take the negativity anymore."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pricey_135-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-pricey-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      However, in an effort to clarify his feelings towards the city of Detroit itself, he wrote and released a poem called "Courageous Dream's Concern."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pricey_135-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-pricey-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In it, he expresses his affection for his hometown.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mccollum_16-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-mccollum-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pricey_135-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-pricey-135">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        135
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      During their 2013 divorce proceedings, Elson entered into evidence an e-mail White had sent her that included disparaging remarks about
      <a href="/wiki/The_Black_Keys" title="The Black Keys">
       The Black Keys
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tim_28-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-tim-28">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        28
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
       <a href="#cite_note-136">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        136
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      When asked about the incident in a 2014
      <i>
       Rolling Stone
      </i>
      magazine interview, White stood by the remarks saying, "I'll hear TV commercials where the music's ripping off sounds of mine, to the point I think it's me. Half the time, it's the Black Keys."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jonah_4-9">
       <a href="#cite_note-jonah-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      He later apologized for the comments.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137">
       <a href="#cite_note-137">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        137
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">
       Philanthropy
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      White has provided financial support to institutions in his hometown of Detroit. In 2009, White donated almost $170,000 towards the renovation of the baseball diamond in southwest Detroit's Clark Park.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
       <a href="#cite_note-138">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        138
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Detroit_Masonic_Temple" title="Detroit Masonic Temple">
       Detroit Masonic Temple
      </a>
      was nearly foreclosed on in 2013 after it was revealed that owners owed $142,000 in back taxes.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freep-20130604-JackWhite_139-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-freep-20130604-JackWhite-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      In June 2013, it was revealed that White had footed the entire bill. To thank him for the donation, the temple has decided to rename its second largest theater the Jack White Theater.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-freep-20130604-JackWhite_139-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-freep-20130604-JackWhite-139">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        139
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140">
       <a href="#cite_note-140">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        140
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Recording_Preservation_Foundation" title="National Recording Preservation Foundation">
       National Recording Preservation Foundation
      </a>
      received an inaugural gift of $200,000 from White to use toward restoring and preserving deteriorating sound recordings on media such as reel-to-reel tape and old cylinders.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker_141-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-parker-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The foundation's director, Eric J. Schwartz said the donation demonstrated a "commitment by a really busy songwriter and performer donating both his time on the board, and money to preserve our national song recording heritage."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parker_141-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-parker-141">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        141
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      White also serves on
      <a href="/wiki/National_Recording_Preservation_Board" title="National Recording Preservation Board">
       the foundation's board
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
       <a href="#cite_note-142">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        142
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_.26_nominations">
       Awards &amp; nominations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Awards &amp; nominations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Jack_White" title="List of awards and nominations received by Jack White">
       List of awards and nominations received by Jack White
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      For his various collaborations and solo work, White has won regional, national and international awards, including eleven
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards" title="Grammy Awards">
       Grammy Awards
      </a>
      . He has been nominated for 29. Nashville mayor
      <a href="/wiki/Karl_Dean" title="Karl Dean">
       Karl Dean
      </a>
      awarded White the title of "Nashville Music City Ambassador" in 2011.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
       <a href="#cite_note-143">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        143
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="As_producer">
       As producer
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jack_White&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: As producer">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Third_Man_Records#Discography" title="Third Man Records">
       Third Man Records  Discography
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      White has been the main or sole producer on all of his own work, as well as that of other bands, particularly those on his Third Man Records label. This is a list of his production credits of notable acts.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <i>

         The White Stripes

        The White Stripes
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/De_Stijl_(album)" title="De Stijl (album)">
         De Stijl
